intensive care \u2013 live updates |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2020/apr/06/coronavirus-live-news-boris-johnson-admitted-to-hospital-as-trump-again-touts-hydroxychloroquine |website=The Guardian |date=6 April 2020 |access-date=6 April 2020}}</ref> [[Dominic Raab]] was appointed to deputise for him.<ref name=\"IT Reactions Guardian\" /> Johnson left intensive care on 9&nbsp;April,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-britain-johnson-idUSKCN21R34I |title=UK PM Johnson leaves intensive care, remains under observation |date=9 April 2020 |work=Reuters |access-date=9 April 2020}}</ref> and left hospital three days later to recuperate at [[Chequers]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Boris Johnson discharged from hospital |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-52262012 |publisher=BBC News |date=12 April 2020 |access-date=12 April 2020}}</ref> After a fortnight at Chequers, he returned to Downing Street on 26&nbsp;April and was said to be chairing a government COVID-19 \"[[war cabinet]]\" meeting.<ref>{{cite news |title=Coronavirus: Boris Johnson's return to work 'a boost for the country' |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/amp/uk-politics-52431913 |publisher=BBC News |date=26 April 2020 |access-date=27 April 2020}}</ref> Johnson later said that he had been given [[Oxygen therapy|emergency oxygen]] while in intensive care, and that doctors had made preparations in case of the event of his death.<ref>{{cite web|title=U.K.'s Boris Johnson says doctors prepared to announce his death as he fought COVID-19|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/news/world/u-k-s-boris-johnson-says-doctors-prepared-announce-his-n1198871|date=3 May 2020|access-date=9 November 2021|publisher=NBC News}}</ref>\n\nA [[Dominic Cummings scandal|scandal]] in May 2020 involved Johnson's chief political advisor [[Dominic Cummings]], who made a trip with his family to [[Durham, England|Durham]] during the March 2020 lockdown while experiencing COVID-19 symptoms. Both Cummings and Johnson rejected widespread calls that Cummings resign.<ref>{{cite news|date=26 May 2020|title=A site for sore eyes? How Dominic Cummings put Barnard Castle on the map|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/travel/2020/may/26/a-site-for-sore-eyes-how-dominic-cummings-put-barnard-castle-on-the-map|access-date=27 May 2020|issn=0261-3077}}</ref><ref>{{cite news| date=25 May 2020|title=No 10 'chaos' as 'defiant' PM defends Cummings|publisher=[[BBC News]]|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/blogs-the-papers-52793529|access-date=27 May 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Why Is the U.K. in an Uproar Over a Boris Johnson Adviser's COVID Road Trip?|url=https://slate.com/news-and-politics/2020/05/dominic-cummings-durham-johnson.html|last=Keating|first=Joshua|date=26 May 2020|website=Slate|access-date=27 May 2020}}</ref> Calls for Johnson to dismiss Cummings came from MPs both within and outside the Conservative Party. Johnson's defence of Cummings and his refusal to sack him caused a widespread backlash.<ref>{{cite news|date=24 May 2020|title=Boris Johnson backs Dominic Cummings over lockdown breach|author=Sebastian Payne|url=https://www.ft.com/content/3e3569ca-01b4-40af-b291-747f482bbe9b|archive-url=https://archive.today/20200524185912/https://www.ft.com/content/3e3569ca-01b4-40af-b291-747f482bbe9b|url-status=dead|archive-date=24 May 2020|work=Financial Times|access-date=10 July 2021}}</ref> This resulted in a loss of confidence in the government and specifically its response to the pandemic, referred to as 'the Cummings effect' in a study in ''[[The Lancet]]''. Concerns were raised in the study that this could affect the public's compliance with pandemic restrictions.<ref>{{Cite journal|last1=Fancourt|first1=Daisy|last2=Steptoe|first2=Andrew|last3=Wright|first3=Liam|date=15 August 2020|title=The Cummings effect: politics, trust, and behaviours during the COVID-19 pandemic|journal=[[The Lancet]]|volume=396|issue=10249|pages=464\u2013465|doi=10.1016/S0140-6736(20)31690-1|issn=0140-6736|pmid=32771083|pmc=7613216 |doi-access=free}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Knapton|first=Sarah|date=6 August 2020|title='Dominic Cummings effect' has led to major loss of confidence in Government, study reveals|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/politics/2020/08/06/dominic-cummings-effect-has-led-major-loss-confidence-government/|url-status=live|work=The Telegraph|issn=0307-1235|archive-url=https://archive.today/2020.08.07-112203/https://www.telegraph.co.uk/politics/2020/08/06/dominic-cummings-effect-has-led-major-loss-confidence-government/|archive-date=7 August 2020|access-date=5 May 2021|url-access=limited}}</ref>\n\nThe Johnson ministry has been [[Controversies regarding COVID-19 contracts in the United Kingdom|accused of cronyism in their assignment of contracts]] related to the pandemic response. process.<ref name=\"PogCal\">{{cite news |last1=Pogrund |first1=Gabriel |last2=Calver |first2=Tom |date=15 November 2020 |title=Chumocracy first in line as ministers splash Covid cash for the whole of England was introduced on 6&nbsp;January 2021.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-55554550 |title=Covid: England's third national lockdown legally comes into force quarantine procedures on arrival.<ref>{{Cite news|date=26 January 2021|title=UK Covid deaths: Why the 100,000 toll is so bad|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/health-55757790|access-date=26 26&nbsp;January.<ref>{{Cite news|date=26 January 2021|title=Covid deaths: UK passes milestone of 100,000|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-55814751|access-date=26 January 2021}}</ref>\n[[File:Boris Johnson greets Joe Biden before the G7 Cornwall Summit.jpg|thumb|Johnson with US President [[Joe Biden]] at the [[47th G7 summit|G7 summit]] in [[Cornwall]], 10 June 2021]]\nIn July 2021, Johnson announced that most generalised public health restrictions in England would be lifted and replaced by recommendations. This took place despite an increase in cases driven by the [[SARS-CoV-2 Delta variant|Delta variant]].<ref>{{cite web|date=12 July 2021|title=Johnson: England to lift last virus restrictions on July 19|url=https://apnews.com/article/europe-business-health-government-and-politics-coronavirus-pandemic-3776cfdb1c180720b9ea000a2c65618b|access-date=9 November 2021|website=AP News}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last=Ellyatt|first=Holly|date=19 July 2021|title=England takes leap into the unknown, lifting Covid rules as cases surge|url=https://www.cnbc.com/2021/07/19/uk-lifts-all-remaining-covid-restrictions-despite-cases-surging.html|access-date=9 November 2021|publisher=[[CNBC]]}}</ref>\n\nIn September 2021, Johnson was pictured in a cabinet meeting, with \"at least 30 people crammed shoulder-to-shoulder\", without anyone wearing masks and with all windows apparently closed, contradicting government advice.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2021/sep/17/boris-johnsons-revamped-cabinet-meet-for-half-time-pep-talk|title=Johnson's revamped cabinet cram into office \u2013 with no masks|author=Peter Walker|work=The Guardian|date=17 September 2021|access-date=21 September 2021}}</ref> Johnson was also photographed without a face mask during a visit to a hospital in November, although images showed that he did wear a mask at some points during his visit.<ref>{{Cite news|title=Dominic Raab defends Boris Johnson after PM is pictured not wearing mask on hospital visit|url=https://news.sky.com/story/dominic-raab-defends-boris-johnson-after-pm-is-pictured-not-wearing-mask-on-hospital-visit-12464422|access-date=9 November 2021|publisher=Sky News}}</ref>\n\nIn December 2021, more stringent restrictions for England were put forward by Johnson and the government. The restrictions, called \"Plan B\", were a partial renewal of previous measures due to the increased incidence of the [[SARS-CoV-2 Omicron variant]]. These proposals included face coverings to be required in more public settings, guidance to [[work from home]] wherever possible, and requirements of [[COVID passports in the United Kingdom|COVID-19 passports]] to enter a nightclub or other large venues.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Gillett |first1=Francesca |last2=Lee |first2=Dulcie |title=Covid: New Plan B rules on working from home and masks announced for England |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-59585307 |work=[[BBC News]] |date=8 December 2021}}</ref> Against these measures, the government experienced the largest rebellion of Conservative MPs during Johnson's premiership.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Swinford |first1=Steven |last2=Zeffman |first2=Henry |title=Johnson suffers biggest rebellion of premiership |url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/johnson-pushes-through-plan-b-despite-largest-rebellion-of-his-premiership-jxw0hq3gg |work=The Times |url-access=limited |date=14 December 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Penna |first1=Dominic |last2=Fisher |first2=Lucy |last3=Nanu |first3=Maighna |title=Politics latest news: Boris Johnson suffers huge rebellion as MPs vote in favour of Covid passports |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/politics/2021/12/14/boris-johnson-news-covid-vaccine-passport-vote-tory-rebellion/ |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20220110/https://www.telegraph.co.uk/politics/2021/12/14/boris-johnson-news-covid-vaccine-passport-vote-tory-rebellion/ |archive-date=10 January 2022 |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |work=The Telegraph |date=14 December 2021}}{{cbignore}}</ref>\n\n====Departure of Dominic Cummings and Lee Cain====\n{{See also|Dominic Cummings scandal|Dominic Cummings#Departure from Downing Street}}\nOn 12&nbsp;November 2020, [[Downing Street Director of Communications]] [[Lee Cain]] resigned amid infighting within the cabinet. He had been offered a promotion to [[Downing Street Chief of Staff|chief of staff]] before his departure.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-54907188 |title=Lee Cain: Top Boris Johnson aide quits amid infighting at No. 10 |work=BBC News |date=12 November 2020 |access-date=29 May 2021}}</ref> On 13&nbsp;November, Johnson ordered Chief Adviser [[Dominic Cummings]], a longtime colleague of Cain, to vacate Downing Street. Despite this, reports stated Cummings and Cain would continue to [[work from home]] for the cabinet office until mid-December.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/nov/13/dominic-cummings-has-already-left-job-at-no-10-reports |title=Boris Johnson boots out top adviser Dominic Cummings |first1=Peter |last1=Walker |first2=Dan |last2=Sabbagh |first3=Rajeev |last3=Syal |work=The Guardian |date=13 November 2020 |access-date=29 May 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite web \"unfit for the job\" and that \"tens of thousands of people died who didn't need to die\" during the early days of the COVID-19 pandemic due to what he claimed to be \"criminal, disgraceful behaviour\" within Downing Street under the supervision of [[Secretary of State for Health and Social Care|Health Secretary]] [[Matt Hancock]].<ref>{{cite news was \"only killing 80-year-olds\" during the pandemic's early stages.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2021/may/26/boris-johnson-refuses-deny-dismissing-covid-scare-story |title=Boris Johnson refuses to deny dismissing Covid as 'scare story' |first=Peter |last=Walker |work=The Guardian |date=26 May 2021 |access-date=29 May 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite web 2021}}</ref>\n\n====Legislative agenda====\nAt the [[2021 State Opening of Parliament|State Opening of Parliament on 11&nbsp;May 2021]], a range of proposed laws were announced that are expected to be enacted during Johnson's second term. These measures include the [[Dissolution and Calling of Parliament Bill]], which would restore the [[royal prerogative]] to dissolve Parliament; a [[Higher Education (Freedom of Speech) Bill]] to combat [[deplatforming]] at universities;<ref name=\"Metro 11-05-2021\">{{cite news|url=https://metro.co.uk/2021/05/11/queens-speech-2021-all-the-new-laws-unveiled-in-the-queens-speech-today-14556784/|last=Brown|first=Faye|date=11 May 2021|title=All the new laws unveiled in the Queen's Speech today|work=Metro|access-date=1 June 2021|archive-date=2 June 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210602213816/https://metro.co.uk/2021/05/11/queens-speech-2021-all-the-new-laws-unveiled-in-the-queens-speech-today-14556784/|url-status=live}}</ref> an [[Online Safety Bill]] that would impose a statutory [[duty of care]] on online companies and empower [[Ofcom]] to block particular websites;<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/technology-57071977|title=Government lays out plans to protect users online|work=[[BBC News]]|last=Wakefield|first=Jane|date=12 May 2021|access-date=12 May 2021|archive-date=12 May 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210512020234/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/technology-57071977|url-status=live}}</ref> and an [[Animal Welfare (Sentience) Bill]] that would legally recognise animal sentience. Further laws would introduce [[voter identification laws|mandatory voter identification]] at general elections, reform the national immigration system, and implement a [[Levelling up policy of the Boris Johnson government|levelling up policy]] to reduce imbalances between areas.<ref name=\"Metro 11-05-2021\" />\n\n====2021 Downing Street refurbishment controversy====\n{{See|2021 Downing Street refurbishment controversy}}\nIn April 2021, Cummings made allegations that Johnson had arranged for donors to \"secretly pay\" for renovations on the private residence at 11 Downing Street.<ref possibly illegal\" and \"almost certainly broke the rules on proper disclosure of political donations if conducted in the way he intended.\"<ref>{{cite news |last1=Walker |first1=Peter Secretary, [[Simon Case]], to hold a review about the refurbishment.<ref>{{Cite news|date=27 April 2021|title=Boris Johnson's flat: Top official to review funding of revamp|work=[[BBC 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210429002311/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2021/apr/28/electoral-commission-launches-inquiry-into-boris-johnson-flat-refurb|url-status=live}}</ref> On the same day Johnson said that he had not broken any laws over the refurbishment and had met the requirements he was obliged to meet in full.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Wright|first1=Oliver|last2=Swinford|first2=Steven|last3=Zeffman|first3=Henry|date=29 April 2021|title=Downing St concern at 'paper trail' over Boris Johnson's flat redecoration|work=[[The Times]]|url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/downing-st-concern-at-paper-trail-over-boris-johnsons-flat-redecoration-qg8vjqj2z|url-status=live|url-access=subscription|access-date=29 April 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210428231545/https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/downing-st-concern-at-paper-trail-over-boris-johnsons-flat-redecoration-qg8vjqj2z|archive-date=28 April 2021}}</ref> During [[Prime Minister's Questions]], the leader of the opposition, [[Keir Starmer]], asked: \"Who ''initially'' paid for the redecoration of his Downing Street flat?\"; Johnson responded: \"I paid for Downing Street's refurbishment personally.\"<ref>{{cite web |title=Commons Chamber 28th April 2021 |url=https://hansard.parliament.uk/Commons/2021-04-28/debates/1e6e4033-a1be-4b3c-ab2c-e35376c9a748/CommonsChamber |website=UK Parliament |access-date=30 April 2021 |archive-date=30 April 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210430111347/https://hansard.parliament.uk/Commons/2021-04-28/debates/1e6e4033-a1be-4b3c-ab2c-e35376c9a748/CommonsChamber |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nOn 28 May [[Christopher Geidt, Baron Geidt|Lord Geidt]] published a report on the allegations in an annex to the [[register of interests]]. The report concluded that Johnson did not breach the Ministerial Code and that no conflict, or reasonably perceived conflict, of interest arose. However, Lord Geidt expressed that it was \"unwise\" for Johnson to have proceeded with refurbishments without \"more rigorous regard for how this would be funded\".<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Walker|first1=Peter|last2=Allegretti|first2=Aubrey|date=28 May 2021|title=Boris Johnson acted unwisely over flat refurbishment, report finds|work=[[The [[Labour Party (UK)|Labour Party]], wrote to Lord Geidt asking for evidence of the lack of conflict of interest and said that it was \"frankly scarcely believable\" that Johnson did not know who was funding the refurbishments.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Skopeliti|first=Clea|date=29 May 2021|title=Angela Rayner demands detailed answers on Boris Johnson's refurb|work=[[The Electoral Commission reported on 9 December that it found that the Conservative Party had failed to follow the law in not accurately reporting donations to the party from Lord Brownlow and imposed a \u00a317,800 fine on the party.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Quinn|first=Ben|date=9 December 2021|title=Downing Street refurb: the money trail, inquiries and questions still to answer|work=The ''[[The Herald (Glasgow)|The Herald]]'' say the commission's report outlines how in March all the money paid by Brownlow and his company had been reimbursed as had payments made by the Conservative Party and Cabinet Office.<ref name=\":1a\" /> Downing Street had said at the time that the full cost of the works had been met personally by the prime minister.<ref name=\":1a\" />\n\n====2021 energy crisis====\nIn September 2021, a [[2021 United Kingdom fuel supply crisis|fuel supply crisis]] occurred in the UK, caused by panic buying triggered by media reports of a leaked government briefing discussing the shortage of [[Large goods vehicle|heavy goods vehicle]] (HGV) drivers.<ref>{{cite news |title=As fuel pumps remain dry, UK's Johnson says plans in place for supply chains |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/uk/uk-puts-military-standby-panic-buying-hits-fuel-supplies-2021-09-27/ |work=Reuters |date=29 September 2021 |access-date=30 July 2022 |archive-date=28 September 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210928201739/https://www.reuters.com/world/uk/uk-puts-military-standby-panic-buying-hits-fuel-supplies-2021-09-27/ |url-status=live }}</ref> This coincided with a [[2021 United Kingdom natural gas supplier crisis|rise in energy prices]] that Johnson said was a \"short-term\" problem caused by \"the global economy coming back to life\" after the COVID-19 pandemic. Economists of various political views, and the head of energy regulator [[Ofgem]] strongly disagreed.<ref>{{cite news |title=Boris Johnson dismisses fears over tough winter |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-58641114 |work=BBC News |date=21 September 2021 |access-date=30 July 2022 |archive-date=6 October 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211006200235/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-58641114 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite news |title=Boris Johnson calls inflation fears 'unfounded' but economists disagree |last=Isaac |first=Anna |work=The Independent |date=5 October 2021 |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/business/news/boris-johnson-news-energy-prices-b1932919.html |access-date=30 July 2022 |archive-date=4 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220704055941/https://www.independent.co.uk/news/business/news/boris-johnson-news-energy-prices-b1932919.html |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\n====2021 Party conference speech====\nAt the Conservative party conference in October 2021, Johnson was criticised by [[Simon Wolfson]], chairman of [[Next plc]], a major party donor and Brexit supporter. Wolfson said Johnson had failed to address supply chain issues. The [[Adam Smith Institute]] described Johnson's speech as \"bombastic but vacuous and economically illiterate\".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/business/2021/oct/06/business-leaders-pm-tory-conference-speech-boris-johnson|title='Economically illiterate': PM's Tory conference speech gets frosty reception|date=6 October 2021|work=The Guardian|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=30 July Paterson controversy====\n{{See also|Owen Paterson#Lobbying and breach of Commons advocacy rules|United Kingdom parliamentary second jobs controversy}}\nIn November 2021, Johnson backed a motion to block the suspension of [[Owen Paterson]], a Conservative MP found to have abused his position by the [[Parliamentary Commissioner for Standards|independent standards commissioner]] after undertaking paid lobbying on behalf of two companies.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Maclellan |first1=Kylie |title=UK PM's party slammed for backing overhaul of system that polices lawmakers |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/uk/uk-parliament-votes-shake-up-rules-halt-suspension-conservative-lawmaker-2021-11-03/ |access-date=4 November 2021 |work=Reuters |date=3 November 2021 |archive-date=30 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220730052615/https://www.reuters.com/world/uk/uk-parliament-votes-shake-up-rules-halt-suspension-conservative-lawmaker-2021-11-03/ |url-status=live }}</ref> The motion called for the creation of a new Conservative-majority committee to examine reforms of the standards investigation process.<ref>{{cite news |title=Owen Paterson: Anger as Tory MP avoids suspension in rule shake-up |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59154221 |access-date=4 November 2021 |work=BBC News |date=3 November 2021 |archive-date=4 November 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211104004818/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59154221 |url-status=live }}</ref> Many Conservative MPs refused to support the motion, and 13 defied a [[Whip (politics)#United Kingdom|three-line whip]] to vote against it.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Woodcock |first1=Andrew |title=Tories vote to tear up sleaze rules after MP found guilty of paid lobbying |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/owen-paterson-commons-sleaze-standards-b1950763.html |access-date=4 November 2021 |work=The Independent |date=3 November 2021 |archive-date=4 November 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211104002315/http://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/owen-paterson-commons-sleaze-standards-b1950763.html |url-status=live }}</ref> Following the announcement by opposition parties that they would boycott the new committee, and faced with a backlash in the media and from MPs of all parties, the government reversed its position and announced that a new vote would take place on whether Paterson should be suspended.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59163961 |title=Owen Paterson row: Government U-turn over MPs' conduct plan |work=BBC News |publisher=[[BBC]] |date=4 November 2021 |access-date=4 November 2021 |archive-date=4 November 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211104105140/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59163961 |url-status=live }}</ref> Paterson announced his resignation as an MP the same day.<ref>{{cite news |title=Tory MP Owen Paterson resigns amid standards row |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59167783 |access-date=4 November 2021 |work=BBC News |date=4 November 2021 |archive-date=4 November 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211104144530/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59167783 |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nAfter Paterson resigned, a [[2021 North Shropshire by-election|by-election]] was held in Paterson's former constituency of [[North Shropshire (UK Parliament constituency)|North Shropshire]]. The [[Liberal Democrats (UK)|Liberal Democrat]] candidate, [[Helen Morgan (politician)|Helen Morgan]], overturned a Conservative majority of nearly 23,000 to win the seat.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-shropshire-59693102 |title=Tories lose North Shropshire seat they held for nearly 200 years |work=[[BBC News]] |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211217084843/http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-shropshire-59693102 |archive-date=17 December 2021 |url-status=live}}</ref> The 34% swing was [[United Kingdom by-election records#Largest swings|seventh largest in United Kingdom by-election history]].<ref>{{Cite }}</ref>\n\n====Partygate scandal====\n{{main|Partygate}}\n[[File:Christmas 2019 Downing Street Decoration (1).jpg|thumb|Downing Street, where some of the gatherings took place<ref name=\"bbc12/4/2022\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dhGDfeo8pRM|title=Partygate: UK PM and chancellor apologise for breaking law in lockdown \u2013 BBC News|via=YouTube|access-date=30 reports emerged that [[Partygate|social gatherings of government and Conservative Party staff]] in Downing Street had taken place ahead of Christmas 2020 against COVID-19 regulations. Johnson and a spokesperson denied these allegations.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Stone |first1=Jon |title=Boris Johnson says 'rules were followed' at No 10 party as Sunak denies attending |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/boris-johnson-rishi-sunak-downing-street-party-b1971373.html |work=The Independent |date=7 December 2021 |access-date=30 July 2022 |archive-date=25 May 2022 |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20220525/https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/boris-johnson-rishi-sunak-downing-street-party-b1971373.html |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Cheese and wine? UK PM's staff joked about alleged lockdown party |url=https://www.reuters.com/world/uk/covid-rules-were-not-broken-downing-street-party-uks-johnson-says-2021-12-07/ |work=Reuters |date=7 December 2021 |access-date=30 July 2022 |archive-date=31 May 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220531100830/https://www.reuters.com/world/uk/covid-rules-were-not-broken-downing-street-party-uks-johnson-says-2021-12-07/ |url-status=live }}</ref> Following a leaked video showing Downing Street staff joking about a \"fictional party\", at a press conference rehearsal recorded days after one alleged party took place, Johnson apologised for the contents of the video and suggested he had been misled but had now ordered an inquiry into whether a party took place and whether rules were broken.<ref>{{cite news |title=PM accused of lying after No 10 officials caught joking about Christmas party |last1=Walker |first1=Peter |last2=Allegretti |first2=Aubrey |last3=Grierson |first3=Jamie |date=7 December 2021 |work=The Guardian |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2021/dec/07/leaked-video-shows-no-10-officials-joking-about-holding-christmas-party |access-date=9 December 2021 |archive-date=9 December 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211209002840/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2021/dec/07/leaked-video-shows-no-10-officials-joking-about-holding-christmas-party |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|date=8 December 2021|title=PMQs: Boris Johnson sorry for offence caused by aides joking about lockdown party|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-59580640|access-date=8 December 2021|archive-date=8 December 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211208121845/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-59580640|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nOn 10 January 2022, [[ITV News]] reported that a planned party had taken place on 20 May 2020, during the first lockdown. ITV had obtained an email sent by principal private secretary [[Martin Reynolds (civil servant)|Martin Reynolds]] to staff inviting them to \"socially distanced drinks\" in the garden of No. 10 and asking them to \"bring your own booze\".<ref name=\"BYOB\">{{cite news |url=https://www.itv.com/news/2022-01-10/email-proves-downing-street-staff-held-drinks-party-at-height-of-lockdown |last=Brand |first=Paul |title=Email proves Downing Street staff held drinks party at height of lockdown |work=ITV News |date=10 January 2022 |access-date=12 January 2022 |archive-date=20 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220120084744/https://www.itv.com/news/2022-01-10/email-proves-downing-street-staff-held-drinks-party-at-height-of-lockdown |url-status=live }}</ref> At the time, people outdoors were not allowed to meet more than one person from outside their household.<ref name=\"sky12/1/2022\">{{cite news |url=https://news.sky.com/story/downing-street-lockdown-party-what-were-the-covid-rules-on-20-may-2020-and-how-many-cases-were-there-12513487 |last=Keay |first=Lara |title=What were the rules on 20 May 2020, what happened in Downing Street, and was Boris Johnson at the party? |publisher=Sky News |date=12 January 2022 |access-date=12 January 2022 |archive-date=11 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220111124233/https://news.sky.com/story/downing-street-lockdown-party-what-were-the-covid-rules-on-20-may-2020-and-how-many-cases-were-there-12513487 |url-status=live }}</ref> Two eyewitnesses later alleged that Johnson and Symonds attended, contradicting Johnson's insistence in December 2021 that there were \"no parties\".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-59946784 |title='Is this for real?' No escape for No 10 from party claims |date=10 January 2022 |work=BBC News |access-date=12 January 2022 |archive-date=11 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220111182500/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-59946784 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name=\"BYOB\"/> At first, Johnson did not deny that he attended.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59957520 |title=No. 10 staff intervened to stop Downing Street events |date=11 January 2022 |work=BBC News |access-date=12 January 2022 |archive-date=12 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220112010623/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59957520 |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nOn 12 January 2022, Johnson apologised to MPs in the Commons for \"attending an event in the Downing Street garden during the first lockdown\",<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59961535 |title=Downing Street party: PM to face MPs following revelations |date=12 January 2022 |work=BBC News |access-date=12 January 2022 |url-status=live |archive-date=12 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220112024830/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-59961535 }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/jan/12/boris-johnson-admits-attending-downing-street-party-during-lockdown |last1=Walker |first1=Peter |last2=Stewart |first2=Heather |title=Boris Johnson admits attending Downing Street party during lockdown |work=The Guardian |date=12 January 2022 |access-date=12 January 2022 |url-status=live |archive-date=12 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220112122819/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/jan/12/boris-johnson-admits-attending-downing-street-party-during-lockdown }}</ref> stating he believed it was \"a work event\".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.itv.com/news/2022-01-12/johnson-faces-demands-to-come-clean-over-bring-your-own-booze-party |title=Boris Johnson admits he attended MPs should await the outcome of the independent inquiry into Westminster lockdown parties, led by senior civil servant [[Sue Gray (civil servant)|Sue Gray]], which he said \"will report as soon as possible\".<ref name=\"CTQ\"/> There were immediate calls across the House for Johnson to resign, voiced mainly by the leaders of the opposition parties. Later, Scottish Conservative leader [[Douglas Ross (Scottish politician)|Douglas Ross]] and several other Conservative MPs expressed their agreement.<ref name=\"CTQ\">{{Cite news|date=12 January 2022|title=Boris Johnson faces calls to quit after lockdown party apology |work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-59967930|access-date=12 January 2022|archive-date=12 January 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220112124556/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-59967930|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=\"bbc12/1/2022\">{{Cite news|date=13 January 2022 |title=Boris Johnson: Senior Tories urge PM to quit after party apology|work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-59972859|url-status=live|archive-date=27 July 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220727161206/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-59972859}}</ref>\n[[File:Sue Gray report Fig 9.jpg|thumb|An image of Johnson at a social gathering, from [[Sue Gray's report]] into the [[partygate]] scandal.]]\nOn 19 January, [[Bury South (UK Parliament constituency)|Bury South]] MP [[Christian Wakeford]] defected from the Conservative Party to the Labour Party.<ref>{{cite news |title=Bury South MP Christian Wakeford resigns from Conservative to join Labour |url=https://www.burytimes.co.uk/news/19858532.bury-south-mp-christian-wakeford-resigns-conservative-join-labour/ |work=Bury Times |date=19 January 2022 |access-date=19 January 2022 |archive-date=19 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220119115747/https://www.burytimes.co.uk/news/19858532.bury-south-mp-christian-wakeford-resigns-conservative-join-labour/ |url-status=live }}</ref> At the end of Prime Minister's Questions, Conservative former minister [[David Davis (British politician)|David Davis]] called for Johnson to resign, quoting [[Leo Amery]] calling on [[Neville Chamberlain]] to resign during the [[Norway Debate]] in 1940, and saying: \"You have sat there too long for all the good you have done. In the name of God, go.\"<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/david-davis-boris-johnson-pmqs-b1996225.html |title='In the name of God, go': Tory MP David Davis tells Boris Johnson to quit |first=Rob |last=Merrick |work=The Independent |date=19 January 2022 |access-date=19 January 2022 |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20220525/https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/david-davis-boris-johnson-pmqs-b1996225.html |archive-date=25 May 2022 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/live/uk-politics-60046632 |title=Boris Johnson: Tory MP defects as ex-minister tells Johnson to go |work=BBC News |date=19 January 2022 |access-date=19 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220119110911/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/live/uk-politics-60046632 |archive-date=19 January 2022 |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |date=19 January 2022 |title=The story behind David Davis's 'In the name of God, go' quote |url=https://inews.co.uk/news/politics/in-the-name-of-god-go-meaning-leo-amery-neville-chamberlain-quote-david-davis-boris-johnson-1411614 |access-date=19 April 2022 |website=inews.co.uk |url-status=live |archive-date=19 April 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220419193936/https://inews.co.uk/news/politics/in-the-name-of-god-go-meaning-leo-amery-neville-chamberlain-quote-david-davis-boris-johnson-1411614 }}</ref> Amery's call was itself a reference to Cromwell's dismissal of the [[Rump Parliament#Oliver Cromwell|Rump parliament]].\n\nOn 25 January, the [[Metropolitan Police]]'s chief commander, [[Cressida Dick]], announced that they were commencing investigations into the Downing Street Parties. Dick stated that \"potential breaches of COVID-19 regulations\" at Downing Street and [[Whitehall]] over the last two years would be looked into.<ref>{{cite news |title=Police to investigate No 10 lockdown parties |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-60123850 |access-date=25 January 2022 |date=25 January 2022 |archive-date=25 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220125101652/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-60123850 |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nAn abbreviated version of the [[Sue Gray report]] into the controversy was released on 31 January, where Gray concluded there was a \"failure of leadership\" over the events that she had examined. The release of the full report was delayed pending the Metropolitan Police's investigation.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-60210893 |title=Sue Gray: No 10 pledges updated report after police inquiry finishes |work=BBC News |publisher=BBC |date=31 January 2022 |access-date=3 February 2022 |url-status=live |archive-date=3 February 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220203165526/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-60210893 }}</ref>\n\nIn early February 2022, four of Johnson's senior aides resigned: [[Dan Rosenfield]] (chief of staff), [[Martin Reynolds (civil servant)|Martin Reynolds]] (principal private secretary), [[Munira Mirza]] (head of policy) and [[Jack Doyle (journalist)|Jack Doyle]] (director of communications).<ref>{{cite news |last1=Zeffman |first1=Henry |editor1-last=Wright |editor1-first=Oliver |editor2-last=Swinford |editor2-first=Steven |title=Crisis for Boris Johnson as four aides quit |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nOn 12 April 2022, Downing Street confirmed that Johnson would be issued a [[fixed penalty notice]] for \u00a350 as police believed he had broken the law by breaching COVID-19 regulations when attending parties during COVID-19 restrictions.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/apr/12/boris-johnson-and-rishi-sunak-fined-for-breaking-covid-lockdown-laws |title=Boris Johnson defies calls to quit after he and Rishi Sunak fined At least 50 such notices would be issued, with other recipients including Johnson's wife and Chancellor Sunak. Johnson therefore became the first Prime Minister in British history to have been sanctioned for breaking the law while in office.<ref name=\":62\">{{cite news |last=Scott |first=Jennifer |date=12 April 2022 |title=Boris Johnson and Rishi Sunak to be fined over lockdown parties |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-61083402 |access-date=12 April 2022 |archive-date=12 April 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220412124621/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-61083402 |url-status=live }}</ref> Boris Johnson either knowingly broke the law or did not understand laws he himself had introduced.<ref name=\"bbc12/4/2022\"/>\n\nAccording to Downing Street insiders, Johnson was involved in instigating a party on the occasion of [[Lee Cain]] leaving Number 10. What had begun as press office drinks became a party after Johnson arrived, gave a speech and poured drinks for staff. [[Labour Party (UK)|Labour]]'s deputy leader, [[Angela Rayner]] said, \"If the latest reports are true, it would mean that not only did the prime minister attend parties, but he had a hand in instigating at least one of them. He has deliberately misled the British people at every turn. The prime minister has demeaned his office.\"<ref>{{cite news |last1=Wheeler |first1=Caroline |last2=Yorke |first2=Harry |location=London |title=Boris Johnson has cleared so many hurdles, but he may Baker added, \"I have to acknowledge that if the prime minister occupied any other office of senior responsibility... he would be long gone.\"<ref>{{cite news|last=Ford Rojas|first=John-Paul|date=21 April 2022|title='The gig's up': Senior Tory backbencher Steve Baker says PM should be 'long gone'|url=https://news.sky.com/story/the-gigs-up-senior-tory-backbencher-steve-baker-says-pm-should-be-long-gone-12595026|work=Sky News|access-date=10 July 2022|archive-date=16 July 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220716130711/https://news.sky.com/story/the-gigs-up-senior-tory-backbencher-steve-baker-says-pm-should-be-long-gone-12595026|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nIn April 2022, a poll by ''[[The Independent]]'' found 27% of voters who voted Conservative in the 2019 general election claim they are less likely vote that way again if Johnson stays leader. Labour were at 40% with the Conservatives at 34%. Johnson rated {{hyphen}}28 (33% claim he does a good job and 61% bad) worse than {{hyphen}}19 the previous month. About 65%, including 46% of Conservative voters maintained Johnson should resign if he gets more fixed penalty notices or gets severe criticism in [[Sue Gray's report]] and 63% maintained his apologies were not good enough. Only 28% believed he did not know he was breaking the law during a Downing Street birthday party, while 63%, including 52% of Conservative voters, maintained he was lying.<ref>{{cite news|last=Woodcock|first=Andrew|date=30 April 2022|title=Revolt in true blue Tory seats 'may hasten end for Johnson', as poll shows PM turns voters off|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/elections-boris-johnson-partygate-voters-b2067806.html|work=The Independent|access-date=10 July 2022|archive-date=5 June 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220605140426/https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/elections-boris-johnson-partygate-voters-b2067806.html|url-status=live}}</ref>\nLeaflets for }}</ref>\n\n====Starmer slur controversy====\nWhile speaking in the House of Commons on 31 January 2022, Johnson falsely blamed Starmer for the non-prosecution of serial sex offender [[Jimmy Savile]] when Starmer was [[Director of Public Prosecutions (England and Wales)|Director of Public Prosecutions]] (DPP) in the [[Crown Prosecution Service]] (CPS). Starmer was DPP in the years immediately prior to Savile's death but there is no evidence he was involved in the decision to not have him prosecuted.<ref>{{Cite news|date=3 February 2022|title=No evidence for Boris Johnson's claim about Keir Starmer and Jimmy Savile|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/60213975|access-date=8 February 2022|archive-date=8 February 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220208163011/https://www.bbc.com/news/60213975|url-status=live}}</ref> The claim linking the failure of the CPS to prosecute Savile to Starmer originated in 2018 on the right-wing [[Guido Fawkes (website)|Guido Fawkes]] blog, and was amplified in April 2020 by the far-right [[fake news website]] [[Politicalite]].<ref name=\"Urwin\">{{cite news |last1=Urwin |first1=Rosamund |title=How fake news infected Britain |url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/fake-news-infected-britain-boris-johnson-jimmy-savile-cfmbgmm85 |access-date=20 February 2022 |work=The Sunday Times |url-access=subscription |date=6 February 2022 |quote=The origin of the claim against Starmer is believed to be a 2018 article on the right-wing political website, Guido Fawkes ... According to research by the campaign group [[Hope Not Hate]], searches for \"Starmer\" and \"Savile\" peaked in April 2020 when the far-right fake news website Politicalite published a piece with the headline, \"New leader new danger: Keir Starmer 'helped paedophile Jimmy {{sic|Saville}} evade justice'\". ... [[Marianna Spring|[Marianna] Spring]] says that the Savile claims have melded with the theories of QAnon, an outlandish US conspiracy cult about devil-worshipping paedophiles |archive-date=20 February 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220220150826/https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/fake-news-infected-britain-boris-johnson-jimmy-savile-cfmbgmm85 |url-status=live }}</ref> Johnson received criticism for the comment and his policy adviser, [[Munira Mirza]], resigned three days later, saying in her resignation letter that Johnson had made \"a scurrilous accusation\" against Starmer.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-60250036 |title=Boris Johnson's policy chief Munira Mirza resigns over PM's Savile remarks |work=BBC News |date=3 February 2022 |access-date=9 February 2022 |archive-date=3 February 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220203160235/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-60250036 |url-status=live }}</ref> On 3 February, during an interview with ''[[Sky News]]'', Johnson defended his comments, stating that in 2013, Starmer apologised because the CPS had not investigated Savile; however, Johnson then said: \"I totally understand that he [Starmer] had nothing to do personally with those decisions\".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://news.sky.com/video/boris-johnson-tries-to-clarify-jimmy-savile-slur-against-sir-keir-starmer-after-days-of-criticism-12532185 |title=Boris Johnson tries to 'clarify' Jimmy Savile 'slur' against Sir Keir Starmer after days of criticism |publisher=Sky News |date=3 February 2022 |access-date=9 February 2022 |archive-date=7 February 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220207074643/https://news.sky.com/video/boris-johnson-tries-to-clarify-jimmy-savile-slur-against-sir-keir-starmer-after-days-of-criticism-12532185 |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nOn 7 February, while Starmer and his colleague [[David Lammy]] were leaving Parliament, they were ambushed by a group of people who shouted abuse at Starmer including the words \"traitor\" and \"Jimmy Savile\". Two people, a man and a woman, were arrested after a [[traffic cone]] was thrown at police officers. Johnson tweeted that it was \"absolutely disgraceful\" and thanked the police for acting swiftly.<ref name=\"two-arrested\">{{cite web |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-60294483 |title=Keir Starmer: Two arrested after protesters surround Labour leader |work=BBC News |date=7 February 2022 |access-date=9 February 2022 |archive-date=8 February 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220208012117/http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-60294483 |url-status=live }}</ref> Shayan Sardarizadeh for [[BBC Monitoring]] said that the protest was an attempt to recreate the [[Canada convoy protest|Canadian convoy protests]] in the UK, and noted that the activists' references to [[Magna Carta]] indicated that the protesters were members of the [[sovereign citizen movement]].<ref name=\"two-arrested\" /> The Savile claims have also been linked to British offshoots of the [[QAnon]] conspiracy movement.<ref name=\"Urwin\" /> [[Julian Smith (politician)|Julian Smith]], the former chief [[Whip (politics)|whip]], and [[Simon Hoare]] were among Conservatives who called for Johnson to apologise. MP [[Kim Leadbeater]] and Brendan Cox, the sister and husband of murdered MP [[Jo Cox]], warned against politicians lending credence to far-right conspiracy theories.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/feb/07/police-rescue-keir-starmer-after-protesters-surround-him-near-parliament |last1=Mason |first1=Rowena |last2=Elgot |first2=Jessica |title=MPs blame Boris Johnson's 'poison' after protesters mob Keir Starmer |work=The Guardian |date=7 February 2022 |access-date=9 February 2022 |archive-date=7 February 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220207223742/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/feb/07/police-rescue-keir-starmer-after-protesters-surround-him-near-parliament |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2022/feb/08/boris-johnson-jimmy-savile-remark-not-apologise |last1=Elgot |first1=Jessica |last2=Stewart |first2=Heather |title=Johnson will not apologise for Jimmy Savile remark, says minister |work=The Guardian |date=8 February 2022 |access-date=9 February 2022 |archive-date=8 February 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220208231530/https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2022/feb/08/boris-johnson-jimmy-savile-remark-not-apologise |url-status=live }}</ref> Death threats sent to Starmer following this episode were later investigated by the police.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2022/feb/13/met-investigates-death-threats-against-keir-starmer-in-wake-of-johnsons-savile-slur |title=Met investigates death threats against Keir Starmer in |archive-date=16 February 2022 |url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n====New hospitals====\nDuring the [[2019 United Kingdom general election]] campaign and many times afterwards, Johnson pledged to build 40 new hospitals by 2030.<ref name=bbc_rc>{{cite news |last1=Barrett |first1=Nicholas |last2=Daniele |first2=Palumbo |date=4 July 2022 |title=What's happened to the 40 new hospitals pledge? |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/59372348 |access-date=4 July 2022 |url-status=live |archive-date=4 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220704162206/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/59372348 }}</ref> Most of the claimed \"new\" hospitals are not entire new hospitals however, but instead new wings or refurbishments of existing hospitals<ref name=bbc_rc/> and only six will be completed by 2025.<ref>{{cite web |title=The government has given six hospitals money to upgrade buildings |url=https://fullfact.org/health/six-hospitals-not-forty/ |website=Full Fact |access-date=4 July 2022 |date=3 October 2019 |archive-date=5 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220705191203/https://fullfact.org/health/six-hospitals-not-forty/ |url-status=live }}</ref> In July 2022 the National Audit Office announced an investigation into the affordability of the pledge and raised concerns about the claim that the hospitals will be \"new\".<ref>{{cite news |last1=Helm |first1=Toby |title=Boris Johnson faces investigation into claims over 40 'new' hospitals |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/jul/02/boris-johnson-faces-investigation-into-claims-over-40-new-hospitals |access-date=4 July 2022 |work=The Guardian |date=2 July 2022 |archive-date=3 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220703210829/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/jul/02/boris-johnson-faces-investigation-into-claims-over-40-new-hospitals |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\n====Vote of confidence====\n{{Main|2022 vote of confidence in the Conservative Party leadership of Boris Johnson}}\nIn the week prior to and throughout the [[Platinum Jubilee of Elizabeth II]] in June 2022, it had been speculated that a vote of confidence in Johnson's leadership of the Conservative Party might occur in the near future.<ref>{{cite 2022.</ref>\n\n==== Pincher scandal ====\n{{main|Chris Pincher scandal}}\nGovernment Deputy Chief Whip [[Chris Pincher]] resigned on 30 June 2022, saying he had \"drunk far too much\" the night before at the [[Carlton Club]], a private members' club, in [[St James's]], London, and having \"embarrassed myself and other people\".<ref>{{cite news |date=1 July 2022 |title=Chris Pincher suspended as suspended as a Conservative MP.<ref>{{cite news |date=1 July 2022 |title=Chris Pincher suspended as Tory MP after groping allegation |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-62014765 Johnson joked about him being \"Pincher by name, pincher by nature\" in 2020, leading to calls for Johnson to explain how much he knew about Pincher's behaviour.<ref>{{Cite news |last1=Blewett initially said that Johnson was unaware of any specific complaints against Pincher when he was appointed as deputy chief whip. that Johnson had been made aware of the matter at that time.<ref>{{Cite news |date=5 July 2022 |title=Boris Johnson was made aware of formal Chris Pincher complaint |work=BBC News Mass resignations ====\n{{main|July 2022 United Kingdom government crisis}}\nOn 5 July, Sunak and Javid resigned within minutes of each other,<ref>{{Cite news |date=5 July 2022 |title=Chris Pincher: PM 'bitterly regrets' appointing MP after complaint |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-62054067 |access-date=30 July 2022 |archive-date=21 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220721191931/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-62054067 |url-status=live }}</ref> followed over the next 24 hours by 11 other ministers, as well as Conservative MPs from [[Parliamentary Private Secretary]] and other Government positions, including the [[Solicitor General]], [[Alex Chalk]];<ref name=\"RESIG\">{{cite news |date=6 July 2022 |title=Government resignations: Who has gone, who is staying? |publisher=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-62058278 |access-date=6 July 2022 |archive-date=5 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220705211035/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-62058278 |url-status=live }}</ref> other [[backbencher]]s also withdrew their support for Johnson. Many of the MPs involved stated that the Pincher affair had led them to change their minds on the suitability of Johnson to hold the office of Prime Minister.<ref name=\"RES\">{{cite news was further reported on 6 July that Johnson could face another confidence vote, with members of the 1922 Committee considering changing the rules as soon as that evening to allow this to happen.<ref names as of 15:00, 6 July 2022</ref> As of May 2022, the government comprised 122 ministers.<ref>{{Cite web |last1=Britchfield |first1=Colm |last2=Devine |first2=Dan |last3=Durrant |first3=Tim resignation ====\n[[File:Prime Minister Boris Johnson's statement in Downing Street 7 July 2022.png|thumb|Johnson announcing his pending resignation as [[Leader of the Conservative Party (UK)|Leader of the Conservative Party]]]]\nBy the morning of 7 July, the newly installed [[Chancellor of the Exchequer]], [[Nadhim Zahawi]], publicly stated his belief that Johnson should resign. Within hours, the BBC and other news outlets reported Boris Johnson's intention to resign as Prime Minister, pending a [[July\u2013September 2022 Conservative Party leadership election|party leadership election]] by autumn 2022. Johnson announced his resignation at 12.30 p.m.<ref>{{cite news |last=Amos|first=Owen|date=7 July 2022|title=Boris Johnson resigns: Five things that led to the PM's downfall|publisher=[[BBC News]]|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-62070422|access-date=7 July 2022|archive-date=7 July remained as Prime Minister until September, while the Conservative Party chose a new leader.<ref>{{cite news |date=7 July 2022 |title=Boris Johnson resigns: Johnson will stay on but only as caretaker off by saying \"[[hasta la vista, baby]]\".<ref>{{cite web |title=Terminated Boris Johnson signs off with 'Hasta la vista, baby' in final PMQs was announced that [[Liz Truss]] had won the [[July\u2013September 2022 Conservative Party leadership election|Conservative leadership election]]. She became prime minister the next day, after formally being appointed by Queen Elizabeth II at [[Balmoral Castle]].<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/rishi-sunak-boris-johnson-labour-nhs-balmoral-b2160000.html | title=Truss wins Tory leadership race and faces daunting challenge as PM | website=[[Independent.co.uk]] | date=5 September 2022 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |date=6 September 2022 |title=Liz Truss confirmed as prime minister after meeting Queen at Balmoral \u2013 UK politics live |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/live/2022/sep/06/liz-truss-pm-boris-johnson-queen-cabinet-reshuffle-rishi-sunak-tories- |access-date=6 September 2022 |website=The Guardian}}</ref> During his farewell speech outside 10 Downing Street on 6 September 2022 Johnson referred to the Roman statesman [[Lucius Quinctius Cincinnatus|Cincinnatus]]. Some commentators noted that, while, as Johnson said, Cincinnatus returned to his plough, he was also later recalled to power.<ref>{{cite web|first=Jamie|last=Grierson|date=6 September 2022|title=Boris Johnson likens himself to Roman who returned as dictator|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/sep/06/boris-johnson-likens-himself-to-roman-cincinnatus-who-returned-as-dictator|website=[[The Guardian]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220906132030/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/sep/06/boris-johnson-likens-himself-to-roman-cincinnatus-who-returned-as-dictator|archive-date=6 September 2022|url-status=live}}</ref> As a former Prime Minister, Johnson, with his wife Carrie, had a place of honour at the [[Death and state funeral of Elizabeth II|state funeral of Queen Elizabeth II]] on 19 September 2022.\n\n=== LGBT issues ===\nIn early April 2022, Johnson decided to ban [[conversion therapy]] for sexual orientation but not for [[Transgender rights in the United Kingdom|transgender Britons]], despite previous commitment to end such treatment for all [[LGBT rights in the United Kingdom|LGBT people]]. He defended his decision citing \"complexities and sensitivities\", adding that he thought biological males should not [[Transgender people in sports|compete in women's sport]] and women should have their own changing rooms. In the government's 2017 LGBT survey, five percent of the respondents said they had been offered a form of conversion therapy, with two percent saying they had undergone it. As a result of the transgender exclusion, over 100 organisations pulled out of a planned global equality conference, Safe To Be Me, which had to be abandoned as a result.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Wright |first1=Oliver |date=1 April 2022 |title=Boris Johnson does double U-turn on LGBT conversion therapy ban |url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/boris-johnson-does-double-u-turn-on-lgbt-conversion-therapy-ban-kgbt9n75n |url-status=live |work=The Times |access-date=6 July 2022 |url-access=limited }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Zeffman |first1=Henry |last2=Smyth |first2=Chris |date=6 April 2022 |title=Boris Johnson: Don't let biological males compete in women's sport |work=The Times |url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/javid-claims-excluding-trans-people-from-conversion-therapy-ban-is-sensitive-approach-q2h2g67xv |access-date=6 July April 2022 }}</ref>\n\n=== Environmental policies ===\nIn November 2020, Johnson announced a 10-point plan for a \"green industrial revolution\", which would include an end to the sale of [[petrol]] and [[Diesel engine|diesel]] cars and vans by 2030,{{efn|This was a reduction on the 2035 target set in February that year, which brought forward the previous deadline of 2040.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Pickard |first1=Jim |last2=Campbell |first2=Peter |date=15 November 2020 |title=UK set to ban sale of new petrol and diesel cars from 2030 }}</ref>\n[[File:Vladimir Putin and Boris Johnson at Libya Conference.jpg|thumb|Johnson and Russian President [[Vladimir Putin]] at the [[Libyan peace process|Berlin Conference on Libya]], 19 January 2020]]\n\n==== Chagos dispute ====\nThe United Kingdom and [[Mauritius]] [[Chagos Archipelago sovereignty dispute|dispute]] the sovereignty of the [[Chagos Archipelago]] in the Indian Ocean.<ref>{{cite news|date=27 August 2018|title=Chagos Islands dispute: UK 'threatened' Mauritius|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-45300739|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=23 March 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210323145031/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-africa-45300739|url-status=live}}</ref> In February 2019, the [[International Court of Justice]] in [[The Hague]] issued [[Legal Consequences of the Separation of the Chagos Archipelago from Mauritius in 1965|an advisory opinion stating]] that the UK has an obligation to bring to an end its administration of the Chagos archipelago as rapidly as possible. In June 2020, 30 British MPs \u2013 including Labour, SNP and Liberal Democrats \u2013 signed a letter calling on Prime Minister Johnson to  act immediately on the ICJ ruling. However, the Foreign Office rejected the advisory opinion.<ref>{{cite news|date=18 June 2020|title=Foreign Office quietly rejects International Court ruling to hand back Chagos Islands|work=[[i (newspaper)|inews.co.uk]]|url=https://inews.co.uk/news/politics/foreign-office-quietly-rejects-international-court-ruling-to-hand-back-chagos-islands-450078|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=30 January 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210130042318/https://inews.co.uk/news/politics/foreign-office-quietly-rejects-international-court-ruling-to-hand-back-chagos-islands-450078|url-status=live}}</ref> Johnson disputed Mauritian claims to sovereignty over the Chagos.<ref>{{cite news|date=22 November 2019|title=Corbyn makes Chagos Islands pledge after UK branded 'illegal colonial occupier'|work=[[Belfast Telegraph]]|url=https://www.belfasttelegraph.co.uk/news/uk/corbyn-makes-chagos-islands-pledge-after-uk-branded-illegal-colonial-occupier-38716676.html|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=31 March 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220331172007/https://www.belfasttelegraph.co.uk/news/uk/corbyn-makes-chagos-islands-pledge-after-uk-branded-illegal-colonial-occupier-38716676.html|url-status=live}}</ref>\n[[File:Boris Johnson visited Warsaw, showed solidarity with NATO against Russia's action (5).jpg|thumb|Johnson with Polish troops and Poland's PM [[Mateusz Morawiecki]] in Warsaw, 10 February 2022]]\n\n==== Hong Kong and China ====\nJohnson said in July 2019 that his government would be very \"pro-China\" in an interview with the [[Hong Kong]] broadcaster [[Phoenix TV]]. He voiced support for Chinese President [[Xi Jinping]]'s infrastructure investment effort, the [[Belt and Road Initiative]], and promised to keep the United Kingdom \"the most open economy in Europe\" for [[Economy of China#Chinese investment abroad|Chinese investment]].<ref>{{cite news|date=24 July 2019|title='Pro-China' Boris Johnson 'enthusiastic' about belt and road plan|publisher=[[Yahoo! News]]|url=https://sg.news.yahoo.com/pro-china-boris-johnson-enthusiastic-065100165.html|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=6 April 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220406173456/https://sg.news.yahoo.com/pro-china-boris-johnson-enthusiastic-065100165.html|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nOn 3&nbsp;June 2020, Johnson announced that if China were to continue pursuing the [[Hong Kong national security law]], the UK would offer 350,000 [[Hongkongers|Hong Kong residents]] who are [[British National (Overseas) passport]] holders, and 2.6&nbsp;million other eligible individuals, the chance to move to the UK, with the possibility of later applying for citizenship.<ref>{{cite news|date=1 July 2020|title=Hong Kong: UK makes citizenship offer to residents|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-53246899|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=1 July 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200701143437/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-politics-53246899|url-status=live}}</ref> China accused the UK of interfering in its internal affairs.<ref>{{cite news|date=3 June 2020|title=China warns UK 'interfering' in Hong Kong affairs will 'backfire'|publisher=[[Al Jazeera English|Al Jazeera]]|url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2020/6/3/china-warns-uk-interfering-in-hong-kong-affairs-will-backfire|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=8 June 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220608135240/https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2020/6/3/china-warns-uk-interfering-in-hong-kong-affairs-will-backfire|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nJohnson refused to describe the Chinese government's [[Uyghur genocide|treatment of the Uyghur people]] as \"genocide\", despite use of the term by the United States.<ref name=\"genocide\"/> Johnson\u2019s government argued that genocide should be decided by the International Criminal Court.<ref>{{cite news |title=Johnson Wins U.K. Vote on Genocide Rulings After China Sanctions |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-03-22/johnson-faces-latest-u-k-tory-rebellion-on-uighur-human-rights |work=Bloomberg |date=22 March 2021}}</ref> Nevertheless, he called what is happening to the [[Uyghurs]] in Xinjiang as \"utterly abhorrent\".<ref name=\"genocide\">{{cite news |title=Boris Johnson refuses to back Trump and Biden teams in calling Uighur situation 'genocide' |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/politics/boris-johnson-uighur-muslims-genocide-trump-biden-b1789997.html |work=The Independent |date=20 January 2021}}</ref>\n\nThe UK joined the [[AUKUS]] defence pact with the United States and Australia in September 2021, which was interpreted as aiming to counter Chinese power in the [[Indo-Pacific]] region. The pact was denounced by China<ref>{{Cite news|date=17 September 2021|title=Aukus: China denounces US-UK-Australia pact as irresponsible|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-58582573|access-date=17 February 2022|archive-date=16 September submarine|plans for Australia to procure French submarines]].<ref>{{cite news|date=22 September 2021|title='Donnez-moi un break': Johnson deepens rift with France over defence deal|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/sep/22/aukus-row-boris-johnson-tells-france-donnez-moi-un-break|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=30 July dismissive of this, saying the pact was not intended to be adversarial towards China, and said that French officials should \"''prenez un'' grip about this and ''donnez-moi un'' break\".<ref>{{cite news|last1=Donaldson|first1=Kitty|date=22 September 2021|title=Boris Johnson Mocks French Outrage Over Submarine Spat|publisher=Bloomberg L.P.|url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-09-22/johnson-says-time-for-france-to-get-a-grip-on-submarine-spat?srnd=premium&sref=CIpmV6x8|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=23 September Afghanistan ====\nOn 8 July 2021, the day after saying he was \"apprehensive\" about the future of Afghanistan following what was then the impending withdrawal of US troops, whilst announcing the near completion of British troop withdrawal from Afghanistan, Johnson expressed the view that there was \"no military path to victory for the [[Taliban]]\".<ref>{{Cite news|date=8 July 2021|title=Most of the remaining British troops have left Afghanistan, says Boris Johnson|work=Mint|agency=Agence France-Presse|url=https://www.livemint.com/news/world/most-of-the-remaining-british-troops-have-left-afghanistan-says-boris-johnson-11625747197686.html|access-date=19 August 2021|archive-date=30 July 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220730052616/https://www.livemint.com/news/world/most-of-the-remaining-british-troops-have-left-afghanistan-says-boris-johnson-11625747197686.html|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=\"Taliban\">{{cite news|date=15 August 2021|title=Boris Johnson urges international unity over Taliban as he recalls parliament|work=The few weeks later, following the [[Fall of Kabul (2021)|fall of Kabul to the Taliban]], he blamed the United States for the crisis caused by the [[Withdrawal of United States troops from Afghanistan (2020\u20132021)|withdrawal of U.S. troops from Afghanistan]],<ref>{{cite news|date=16 August 2021|title=Afghanistan crisis: Johnson took holiday as Kabul was about to fall|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2021/aug/16/afghanistan-crisis-pm-boris-johnson-ended-summer-holiday|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=26 June news|date=16 August 2021|title=Blame on Biden? UK PM Johnson says US decision to pull out of Afghanistan 'accelerated' events|work=The Week|url=https://www.theweek.in/news/world/2021/08/16/trouble-for-biden-uk-pm-says-us-decision-to-pull-out-of-afghanista-accelerated-events.html|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=16 August 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210816074255/https://www.theweek.in/news/world/2021/08/16/trouble-for-biden-uk-pm-says-us-decision-to-pull-out-of-afghanista-accelerated-events.html|url-status=live}}</ref> saying that [[NATO]] alliance members \"could not continue this US-led mission, a mission conceived and executed in support of America, without American logistics, without US air power and without American might\".<ref>{{cite news|date=18 August 2021|title=British government details plan to settle 20,000 Afghan refugees in heated emergency debate|publisher=CBC News|url=https://www.cbc.ca/news/world/britain-refugees-afghanistan-1.6144731|access-date=30 July 2022|archive-date=30 July 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220730052618/https://www.cbc.ca/news/world/britain-refugees-afghanistan-1.6144731|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n==== UK\u2013EU trade negotiation ====\n{{Main|Trade deal negotiation between the UK and EU|EU\u2013UK Trade and Cooperation Agreement}}\nFollowing the formal [[Brexit|withdrawal from the European Union]] in January 2020, Johnson's government entered [[Trade negotiation between the UK and the EU|trade negotiations with the EU]] to agree on their future relationship before the end of the [[Brexit transition period|transition period]] on 31 December 2020.<ref name=\":1\">{{Cite news|last1=Mueller|first1=Benjamin|last2=Robins|first2=Peter|date=8 November 2021|title=What Is Brexit? And How Is It Going?|work=The New York Times|url=https://www.nytimes.com/article/brexit-uk-eu-explained.html|access-date=4 February 2022|issn=0362-4331|archive-date=29 December 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201229062101/https://www.nytimes.com/2020/12/24/world/europe/brexit-uk-eu-explained.html|url-status=live}}</ref> [[Fish for finance|Fisheries was a major topic]] of the negotiations.<ref name=\":1\" /><ref>{{Cite news|date=30 December 2020|title='Boris the betrayer' has swindled us over Brexit, England's fishermen say|work=Reuters|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-britain-eu-fish-idUSKBN29415G|access-date=4 February 2022|archive-date=4 February 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220204114610/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-britain-eu-fish-idUSKBN29415G|url-status=live}}</ref> On 16&nbsp;October 2020 Johnson said that the UK \"must get ready\" for no trade deal with the EU.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Sparrow|first=Andrew|date=16 October 2020|title=Boris Johnson: UK must prepare for no-deal Brexit and 'Australia-style' trade \u2013 UK politics live|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/live/2020/oct/16/uk-coronavirus-live-boris-johnson-local-restrictions-lockdown-tier-2-covid-brexit-latest-updates|access-date=16 October 2020|archive-date=16 October 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201016084900/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/live/2020/oct/16/uk-coronavirus-live-boris-johnson-local-restrictions-lockdown-tier-2-covid-brexit-latest-updates|url-status=live}}</ref> With negotiations continuing until days before the deadline, it was announced on 24&nbsp;December 2020 that a trade deal had been agreed.<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Boffey|first1=Daniel|last2=O'Carroll|first2=Lisa|date=24 December 2020 |title=UK and EU agree Brexit trade deal|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/dec/24/uk-eu-agree-brexit-trade-deal-agreement|access-date=3 January 2021|archive-date=29 December 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201229024159/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/dec/24/uk-eu-agree-brexit-trade-deal-agreement|url-status=live}}</ref> Entitled the [[EU\u2013UK Trade and Cooperation Agreement]], it came into force provisionally on 1&nbsp;January 2021, and formally on 1 May. A [[2021 Jersey dispute|fisheries dispute between the UK and France]] occurred shortly afterwards. Introduction of new UK border checks were delayed until 2022 to minimise the disruption caused by the COVID-19 pandemic.<ref name=\":1\" />\n\nIn May 2022, Johnson readied a draft that would unilaterally change parts of the [[Northern Ireland Protocol]], citing issues with medical supplies and cuts in VAT. One of the thornier points of contention involves safety regulations for food and plants, an area where the British government is opposed to a closer alignment with existing EU regulations. For its part, the EU has so far rebuffed the idea of changing the text of the treaty to accommodate the British. A unilateral override by the UK would be tantamount to a breach of the agreement. As Johnson sought a more conciliatory tone, sources within the government began to stress that the draft is designed to be an \"insurance policy\" and in any case would take years to become law.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Smyth |first1=Chris |last2=Waterfield |first2=Bruno |last3=Charter |first3=David |title=Boris Johnson defies warnings over Northern Ireland protocol |url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/boris-johnson-defies-warnings-over-northern-ireland-protocol-mvtskzfvs |date=16 May 2022 |access-date=30 July 2022 |archive-date=5 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220705185157/https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/boris-johnson-defies-warnings-over-northern-ireland-protocol-mvtskzfvs |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\n==== Russia and Ukraine ====\n[[File:President of Ukraine Volodymyr Zelenskyy and Prime Minister of the United Kingdom Boris Johnson walked around the center of Kyiv. (51994084277).jpg|thumb|right|Johnson walks on a street of war-hit [[Kyiv]] along with [[President of Ukraine]] [[Volodymyr Zelenskyy]] on 10 April 2022]]\nIn November 2021, Johnson warned that the European Union faces \"a choice\" between \"sticking up for Ukraine\" and approving the [[Nord Stream 2]] natural gas pipeline which runs from Russia to Europe.<ref>{{cite news |title=Boris Johnson warns EU to choose between Ukraine and Nord Stream 2 |url=https://www.ft.com/content/93c720de-bf39-4803-b1ec-1cd1798431e9 |work=Financial Times |date=15 November 2021 |access-date=30 July 2022 agreed in a phone call to work towards a \"peaceful resolution\".<ref>{{cite news |title=UK, Russian leaders discuss Ukraine crisis in phone call |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\nJohnson condemned the [[2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine]], and ensured the UK joined in [[International sanctions during the 2022 Russian invasion of Johnson [[Web conferencing|virtually addressed]] the [[Verkhovna Rada|Ukrainian parliament]], becoming the first world leader to speak in Ukraine since the invasion. October 2022, Johnson sought support from MPs to run in the subsequent [[October 2022 Conservative Party leadership election|leadership election]], and received support from several cabinet members.<ref name=\"BBC2110\">{{cite news |last1=Francis |first1=Same |title=Could Boris Johnson really make a comeback? |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-63342114 |work=BBC News |access-date=21 October 2022 |date=21 October 2022}}</ref> Three days later, he announced that he would not stand, stating that he would not have enough support from MPs to govern effectively.<ref
