contest|first=Rowena|last=Mason|work=The Guardian|date=23 October 2022|accessdate=23 October 2022}}</ref>\n\n==Political positions and ideology==\n{{main|Political positions of Boris Johnson}}\n[[File:Boris Johnson hartismere.jpg|thumb|Johnson at a demonstration against hospital closures with Liberal Democrat MP [[John Hemming (politician)|John Hemming]] (left) and Conservative MP [[Graham Stuart (politician)|Graham Stuart]] (centre) in March 2006]]\n{{quote box|width=25em|align=right|quote=[I am] free-market, tolerant, broadly libertarian (though perhaps not ultra-libertarian), inclined to see the merit of traditions, anti-regulation, pro-immigrant, pro-standing on your own two feet, pro-alcohol, pro-hunting, pro-motorist and ready to defend to the death the right of [[Glenn Hoddle#Dismissal from England job|Glenn Hoddle to believe in reincarnation]].|author= \u2014Boris Johnson, 2011{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=225}}}}\n\nIdeologically, Johnson has been described by himself and others as a \"[[One-Nation Tory]]\".<ref>{{cite news |last=Ferguson |first=Niall |author-link=Niall Ferguson |title=It's One Nation under Boris Johnson's populist groove |url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/its-one-nation-under-boris-johnsons-populist-groove-s5vqb3vbk |url-status=live |website=[[The Times]] |date=15 December 2019 |access-date=4 January 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201028180329/https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/its-one-nation-under-boris-johnsons-populist-groove-s5vqb3vbk |archive-date=28 October 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Parker |first=George |date=21 December 2014 |title=Boris Johnson aims to win back voters as 'One Nation Tory' |url=https://www.ft.com/content/74339ea2-88f8-11e4-ad5b-00144feabdc0 |url-status=live |work=Financial Times |location=London |archive-url=https://archive.today/2016.12.14-213726/https://www.ft.com/content/74339ea2-88f8-11e4-ad5b-00144feabdc0 |archive-date=14 December 2016 |access-date=5 May 2021 |url-access=subscription}}</ref> Political scientists have described Johnson's political positions as ambiguous and contradictory, encompassing [[Nativism (politics)|nativist]], [[authoritarian]] and [[free market]] tendencies on the one hand, and one-nation [[liberal conservatism]] on the other.<ref name=\"Hayton_2021\" >{{cite journal |last=Hayton |first=Richard |title=Conservative Party Statecraft and the Johnson Government |journal=The Political Quarterly |volume=92 |issue=3 |pages=412\u2013419 |date=July 2021 |s2cid=236571324 |doi=10.1111/1467-923X.13006}}</ref> Some scholars have questioned Johnson's commitment to one-nation conservativism, instead characterising his ideology as being flexible and populist.<ref>{{cite journal |last=Mornington |first=Alicia-Dorothy |title=Was Boris Johnson's One-Nation Post-Electoral Pledge Sincere? |journal=French Journal of British Studies |volume=25 |issue=3 |date=29 June 2020 |s2cid=225755384 |doi=10.4000/rfcb.5693}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last=Williams |first=Ben |title=Boris Johnson \u2013 one nation Conservative or populist? |url=https://www.politicshome.com/thehouse/article/boris-johnson-one-nation-conservative-or-populist |work=Politics Home |date=11 February 2022 |access-date=9 August 2022}}</ref> Purnell stated that Johnson regularly changed his opinion on political issues, commenting on what she perceived to be \"an ideological emptiness beneath the staunch Tory exterior\".{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=2}} She later referred to his \"opportunistic \u2013 some might say pragmatic \u2013 approach to politics\".{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=121}}\n\nDuring his tenure as London Mayor, Johnson gained a reputation as \"a liberal, centre-ground politician\", according to ''[[Business Insider]]''.<ref>{{cite news |title=Conservative moderates plan to take back control of Boris Johnson as prime minister |first1=Adam |last1=Payne |first2=Adam |last2=Bienkov |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/boris-johnson-conservative-leadership-race-moderate-mp-brexit-theresa-may-2019-5?r=US&IR=T |website=[[Business Insider]] |date=23 May 2019 |access-date=26 May 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200406193257/https://www.businessinsider.com/boris-johnson-conservative-leadership-race-moderate-mp-brexit-theresa-may-2019-5?r=US&IR=T |url-status=live |archive-date=6 April 2020}}</ref> In 2012, the political scientist [[Tony Travers]] described Johnson as \"a fairly classic\u2014that is, small-state\u2014mildly [[Euroscepticism in the United Kingdom|eurosceptic]] Conservative\" who, like his contemporaries Cameron and [[George Osborne]], also embraced \"modern social liberalism\".<ref name=\"Channel4\">{{cite news |title=Boris Johnson: Classic Tory or Political Maverick? |work=[[Channel 4 News]] |date=9 October 2012 |url=http://www.channel4.com/news/borish-johnson-classic-tory-or-political-maverick |access-date=26 May 2019 |url-status=live |archive-date=18 March 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150318042522/https://www.channel4.com/news/borish-johnson-classic-tory-or-political-maverick}}</ref> ''[[The Guardian]]'' stated that while mayor, Johnson blended economic and social liberalism,<ref>{{cite news |title=Mayor Boris, the liberal |work=[[The Guardian]] |location=London |last=Hill |first=Dave |date=4 December 2008 |url=https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2008/dec/04/boris-johnson-london-mayor-conservatives |access-date=11 December 2016 |url-status=live |archive-date=11 November 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181111063703/https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2008/dec/04/boris-johnson-london-mayor-conservatives}}</ref> with ''[[The Economist]]'' saying that in doing so Johnson \"transcends his Tory identity\" and adopts a more libertarian perspective.<ref>{{cite news |title=Generation Boris |newspaper=[[The Economist]] |location=London |date=1 June 2013 |url=https://www.economist.com/news/britain/21578666-britains-youth-are-not-just-more-liberal-their-elders-they-are-also-more-liberal-any |url-access=subscription |access-date=5 May 2021 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150103002329/https://www.economist.com/news/britain/21578666-britains-youth-are-not-just-more-liberal-their-elders-they-are-also-more-liberal-any |archive-date=3 January 2015}}</ref>\n\nAccording to political scientist Richard Hayton, Johnson's premiership centred around Brexit, which served as a \"national cause\". Johnson evoked the discourse of [[popular sovereignty]] and [[anti-establishment]] populism to portray Parliament as seeking to \"sabotage\" Brexit, and in doing so, presented himself \"as the true representative of 'the people'\".<ref name=\"Hayton_2021\" /><ref name=\"Alexandre-Collier_2022\" /> In 2019, [[Al Jazeera]] editor James Brownswell said that although Johnson had \"leaned to the right\" since the Brexit campaign, he remained \"slightly more socially liberal\" than much of his party.<ref>{{cite web |last=Brownswell |first=James |title=Who is Boris Johnson, Britain's new prime minister? |publisher=Al Jazeera |date=23 July 2019 |access-date=28 August 2019 |url=https://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/boris-johnson-britain-prime-minister-190722183952925.html |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200101164349/https://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/boris-johnson-britain-prime-minister-190722183952925.html|archive-date=1 January 2020}}</ref>\n\nScholars of [[comparative politics]] have drawn comparisons between Johnson and other populist leaders such as Donald Trump and [[Viktor Orban]].<ref name=\"Alexandre-Collier_2022\" >{{cite journal |last1=Alexandre-Collier |first1=Agn\u00e8s |title=David Cameron, Boris Johnson and the 'populist hypothesis' in the British Conservative Party |journal=Comparative European Politics |date=13 April 2022 |volume=20 |issue=5 |pages=527\u2013543 |doi=10.1057/s41295-022-00294-5|s2cid=248154829 }}</ref> Some commentators have likened aspects of Johnson's political style to [[Trumpism]],<ref name=\":7\">{{cite news |last=Chadwick |first=Vince |date=24 May 2016 |title=Donald Trump and Boris Johnson kiss and make Out |work=[[Politico]] |url=http://www.politico.eu/article/donald-trump-boris-johnson-kiss-mural-brexit-referendum-leave-remain/ |url-status=live |access-date=30 July 2022 name=\":2\">{{cite news |last=Greenslade |first=Roy |author-link=Roy Greenslade |date=29 June 2016 |title=New York Post compares Boris Johnson to Donald Trump |work=The Guardian |location=London |url=https://www.theguardian.com/media/greenslade/2016/jun/29/new-york-post-compares-boris-johnson-to-donald-trump |url-status=live |access-date=30 July 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210206063615/https://www.theguardian.com/media/greenslade/2016/jun/29/new-york-post-compares-boris-johnson-to-donald-trump |archive-date=6 February 2021}}</ref><ref name=\"atlantic202110\">{{Cite web |last=McTague |first=Tom |date=4 October 2021 |title=Is Boris Johnson a Liar? |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211019032011/https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2021/10/boris-johnson/620269/ |archive-date=19 October 2021 |access-date=18 October 2021 |website=The Atlantic}}</ref> although others have argued against this, saying that Johnson's stance on matters such as social policy, immigration and free trade is liberal.<ref>{{cite news |last=Bourne |first=Ryan |date=23 July 2019 |title=Don't lump Boris Johnson together with Donald Trump |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/2019/07/23/dont-lump-boris-johnson-together-with-donald-trump/ |url-status=live |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |archive-url=https://archive.today/2019.07.23-154017/https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/2019/07/23/dont-lump-boris-johnson-together-with-donald-trump/?noredirect=on |archive-date=23 July 2019 |access-date=5 May 2021 |url-access=subscription}}</ref>\n\nJohnson biographer Gimson wrote that Johnson is economically and socially \"a genuine liberal\", although he retains a \"Tory element\" to his personality through his \"love of existing institutions, and a recognition of the inevitability of hierarchy\".{{sfn|Gimson|2012|p=342}} Stuart Reid, Johnson's colleague at ''The Spectator'', described the latter's views as being those of a \"liberal libertarian\".{{sfn|Gimson|2012|p=136}} In 2019, reacting to reports in [[The Sun (United Kingdom)|''The Sun'']], that Johnson had told cabinet colleagues he was \"basically a Brexity Hezza\", former deputy leader of the Conservative Party [[Michael Heseltine]] said Johnson \"has no right to call himself a one-nation Conservative\" and wrote: \"I fear that any traces of liberal conservatism that still exist within the prime minister have long since been captured by the rightwing, foreigner-bashing, inward-looking view of the world that has come to characterise his fellow Brexiters.\"<ref>{{cite news |last=Heseltine |first=Michael |author-link=Michael Heseltine |title=Boris Johnson has no right to call himself a one-nation |archive-date=31 March 2022}}</ref>\n\n===Environment===\n[[File:World Leaders' Summit Opening Ceremony (51647616433).jpg|thumb|Johnson spoke about climate action at the [[2021 United Nations Climate Change Conference|COP26 climate summit]] in Glasgow on 1 November 2021]]\nAccording to [[TheyWorkForYou]], Johnson has \"generally voted against\" what it described as \"measures to prevent [[Climate change in the United Kingdom|climate change]]\" while an MP.<ref name=\"newscientist\">{{cite web|last=Aron|first=Jacob|title=New prime minister Boris Johnson's climate change record|url=https://www.newscientist.com/article/2205441-new-prime-minister-boris-johnsons-climate-change-record/|access-date=1 January 2021|website=[[New Scientist]]|archive-date=24 November name=\":3\">{{cite web|title=What is Boris Johnson's record on climate change?|url=https://www.theweek.co.uk/105521/boris-johnson-s-record-on-climate-change|access-date=18 November 2021|website=The Week UK|archive-date=18 November 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211118152710/https://www.theweek.co.uk/105521/boris-johnson-s-record-on-climate-change|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Boris Johnson London, Johnson expressed [[climate skeptic]]al views in several columns.<ref name=\":0\">{{cite news|date=2 February 2022|title=Climate change: The science briefing that convinced Boris Johnson|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/science-environment-60203674|access-date=2 February 2022|archive-date=2 February Telegraph'' columns published in 2012 and 2013, he conflated the distinction between weather and climate and highlighted a factually incorrect claim by weather forecaster and conspiracy theorist [[Piers Corbyn]] that reduced solar activity could lead to a \"mini-Ice Age\".<ref name=\"newscientist\"/><ref name=\":4\">{{cite news |last=Ward |first=Bob |title=Boris Johnson's climate change \"scepticism\" is an embarrassment to London's scientists |url=https://www.newstatesman.com/politics/2013/01/boris-johnsons-climate-change-scepticism-embarrassment-londons-scientists |access-date=18 [[Bloomberg News]] suggested that Johnson's interest in climate change increased after becoming Prime Minister, and suggested this could have been influenced by his wife [[Carrie Symonds]] and father [[Stanley Johnson (writer)|Stanley Johnson]], who are both environmental campaigners.<ref name=\"bloomberg2\">{{cite news  |title=What Does Boris Johnson Really Think About Climate Change? |publisher=Bloomberg L.P. |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-02-05/what-does-boris-johnson-really-think-about-climate-change |date=5 February 2020 |access-date=1 January 2021 |url-status=live}}</ref> It was reported in 2022 that Johnson was convinced of the [[scientific consensus on climate change]] following a briefing by the chief scientist of the [[Met Office]] in January 2020, and subsequently made the issue a priority for his government.<ref name=\":0\" />\n\nIn 2019 and 2020, Johnson expressed support for the UK to have [[Carbon neutrality|\"net-zero\" greenhouse gas emissions]] by 2050<ref>{{cite news |last=Vaughan |first=Adam |date=11 June 2019 |title=UK commits to reduce greenhouse gas emissions to net zero by 2050 |journal=New Scientist spoke about increasing ambition for mitigating climate change through [[carbon capture and storage]]<ref>{{cite news |last=Gatten |first=Emma |date=24 September 2020 |title=Boris Johnson warns against Boris Johnson|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-59114871|access-date=18 November 2021|archive-date=18 November November 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211117165044/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-59284505 |url-status=live }}</ref>\n\n===Immigration and the European Union===\n[[File:Johnson meets with Junker in Luxembourg.jpg|thumb|Johnson with EU Commission President [[Jean-Claude Juncker]], 16 September 2019]]\nPurnell believed it was the influence of Johnson's maternal family, the left-wing Fawcetts, that led to him developing \"a genuine abhorrence of racial discrimination\".{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=25}} In 2003, Johnson said of the EU, \"I am not by any means an ultra-[[Euroscepticism in the United Kingdom|Eurosceptic]]. In some ways, I am a bit of a fan of the [[European Union]]. If we did not have one, we would invent something like it.\"<ref name=\"businessinsider\"/> As Mayor of London, Johnson was known as a supporter of [[Modern immigration to the United Kingdom|immigration]].<ref name=\"businessinsider\">{{cite web |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/boris-johnson-brexit-speech-changed-his-mind-remain-2018-2 |title=All the times Boris Johnson has contradicted his own arguments for Brexit |first=Adam |last=Bienkov |website=Business Insider |access-date=26 May 2019 |date=14 February 2018 |archive-date=26 May 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190526224707/https://www.businessinsider.com/boris-johnson-brexit-speech-changed-his-mind-remain-2018-2 |url-status=live}}</ref> From 2009, he advocated a referendum on Britain's EU membership.<ref name=\"businessinsider\"/><ref>{{cite journal |last1=Worthy |first1=Ben |last2=Bennister |first2=Mark |last3=Stafford |first3=Max W. |title=Rebels Leading |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190428224218/http://create.canterbury.ac.uk/16760/1/16760_Rebels%20as%20Mayors%20WorthyBennisterStafford%28BP%29.pdf}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url-status=dead |archive-date=18 October 2016 |title=A secret pro-EU article Boris Johnson wrote before the referendum has been revealed |date=15 October 2016 |website=The Independent |access-date=26 May 2019}}</ref>\n\nIn 2018, during the Brexit negotiations, he called for Britain to leave the [[European Single Market|Single Market]]<ref name=\"businessinsider\"/> and advocated a more liberal approach to immigration than that of Prime Minister Theresa May.<ref>{{cite news |last=Ross |first=Tim |date=23 May 2018 |title=Boris Johnson reopens post-Brexit immigration debate |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2018-05-23/boris-johnson-calls-for-welcoming-approach-to-immigration |publisher=Bloomberg |access-date=5 May 2021 |url-access=subscription |archive-date=5 }}</ref> He stated many people believed that [[United Kingdom membership of the European Union|Britain's EU membership]] had led to the suppression of the wages of its \"indigenous\" people and said the EU was intent on creating a \"superstate\" that would seek to rob Britain of its sovereignty.<ref name=\"businessinsider\"/> In 2019, Johnson said he would take Britain out of the EU on 31&nbsp;October whether there was a trade deal in place or not.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2019/may/26/brexit-top-tories-would-bring-down-any-pm-who-backs-no-deal |title=Brexit: top Tories would bring down any PM who backs no deal |last=Mason |first=Rowena |date=26 May 2019 |work=The Guardian |access-date=26 May 2019 |issn=0261-3077 |archive-date=26 May 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190526204831/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2019/may/26/brexit-top-tories-would-bring-down-any-pm-who-backs-no-deal |url-status=live }}</ref> Johnson also stated his opposition to a [[referendum on the Brexit withdrawal agreement]].<ref>{{cite tweet |user=borisjohnson |number=1143536757360738304 |date=25 June 2019 |title=If I become PM, we will leave the EU on 31 October, deal or no deal. Today I have asked @Jeremy_Hunt whether he will also commit to this date, no matter what. We must keep our promises to the British people and deliver Brexit \u2013 no ifs, no buts, and no second referendum.}}</ref>\n\nOn 19 August 2019, Johnson wrote a letter to the EU and asked for the removal of the \"backstop\" accord, which had previously been agreed and signed by Theresa May during her premiership. The president of the European Council, [[Donald Tusk]], rejected the proposal.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.kcbx.org/post/britains-boris-johnson-appeals-eu-drop-irish-backstop-demand#stream/0 |title=Britain's Boris Johnson Appeals To EU To Drop 'Irish Backstop' Demand |access-date=20 August 2019 |work=kcbx.org |date=20 August 2019 |archive-date=10 February 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200210152333/https://www.kcbx.org/post/britains-boris-johnson-appeals-eu-drop-irish-backstop-demand#stream/0 |url-status=live}}</ref> On 26 August 2019, Johnson said that Britain would not pay \u00a339&nbsp;billion for the withdrawal agreement were the UK to leave without a deal on&nbsp;31 October. The European Parliament Brexit coordinator [[Guy Verhofstadt]] said there would be no further negotiation on the trade deal unless the UK agreed to pay the entire sum.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.neweurope.eu/article/johnson-says-britain-will-not-pay-brussels-for-no-deal-brexit/ |title=Johnson says Britain will not pay Brussels for no-deal Brexit |access-date=27 August 2019 |work=New Europe |date=27 August 2019 |archive-date=28 August 2019 inline|date=February 2022}}\n\n===Unionism and devolution===\nSpeaking in [[Northern Ireland]], Johnson described himself as a \"fervent and passionate [[Unionism in the United Kingdom|unionist]]\".<ref>{{cite news |title=Boris Johnson declares unionist views on trip to Northern Ireland |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-northern-ireland-50338539 |access-date=24 November 2020 |work=BBC News |date=7 November 2019 |archive-date=29 November 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201129025339/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-northern-ireland-50338539 |url-status=live}}</ref> He proposed building a [[Irish Sea Bridge|bridge or tunnel between Scotland and Northern Ireland]], but has since scrapped this initiative.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-northern-ireland-58574878.amp |title=Northern Ireland to Scotland bridge plans 'put to bed' |date=15 September 2021 |access-date=23 November 2021 |archive-date=20 November 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211120232421/https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-northern-ireland-58574878.amp |url-status=live}}</ref>\n\nThe devolved administrations have criticised the [[Internal Market Bill]] for its re-centralisation of control over commerce, reversing the [[Devolution in the United Kingdom|devolution of power in the United Kingdom]].<ref>{{cite web |url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n==Public image==\n{{main|Public image of Boris Johnson}}\n[[File:Boris Johnson pulling a bull in Aberdeen.jpg|alt=Boris Johnson pulling a cow.|thumb|Johnson visiting a cattle farm in [[Aberdeen]] in 2019]]Johnson has been described by various biographers and commentators as having a light hearted and charming persona,{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=103}}<ref name=\"Huffpo1e4\">{{cite news |last=Frost |first=Caroline |title=17 Things We Now Know About Boris Johnson, And His Worthiness, Or Not, To Be PM ... |url-status=live}}</ref>{{sfn|Crines|2013|p=1}}{{sfn|Hill|2016|p=31}}{{sfn|Gimson|2012|p=x}} many of whom suggest he has put significant thought and effort into developing this version of himself throughout his adult life.{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=91}}{{sfn|Edwards|Isaby|2008|p=74}}{{sfnm|1a1=Edwards|1a2=Isaby|1y=2008|1p=74|2a1=Purnell|2y=2011|2p=1|3a1=Gimson|3y=2012|3p=301}}{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=3}} He has been noted as making significant use of humour in relation to this, sometimes for explicitly political purposes.{{sfn|Crines|2013|p=1}}{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=214}}{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=26}} Johnson has said that \"humour is a utensil that you can use to sugar the pill and to get important points across\".{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=3}} He is said to have a genuine desire to be liked.{{sfn|Gimson|2012|p=258}} He has also been described, including by some of those that have known him personally, as heavily focused on his own interests,{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=183}}{{sfn|Gimson|2012|p=108}}{{sfn|Gimson|2012|p=17}} with an often vitriolic or irresponsible way of conducting himself in private.{{sfn|Purnell|2011|pp=6\u20137}}{{sfn|Gimson|2012|p=301}}{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=37}}\n\nJohnson has been described as a divisive and controversial figure in British politics.<ref>{{cite news |date=26 May 2019 |title=Who is Boris Johnson, the man poised to be the next British leader? |publisher=NBC News |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/news/world/who-boris-johnson-man-poised-be-next-british-leader-n1009841}}</ref><ref name=\"ABC3\">{{cite news |last=Davies |first=Guy |date=23 July 2019 |title=Meet Boris entertaining.{{sfn|Gimson|2012|p=20}} Johnson has been accused of lying or making untruthful or misleading statements throughout his career,<ref>{{cite news |last=Grierson |first=Jamie |date=10 December 2021 |title=Lies, damned lies: the full list of accusations against Boris Johnson |work=The Guardian |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2021/dec/10/lies-accusations-boris-johnson-full-list-dishonesty-christmas-party |access-date=19 December 2021}}</ref> and has been described as racist and otherwise bigoted;{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=365}} comparisons have been drawn with US president [[Donald Trump]].<ref name=\":72\">{{cite news |last=Chadwick |first=Vince |date=24 May 2016 |title=Donald Trump and Boris Johnson kiss and make Out |work=[[Politico]] |url=http://www.politico.eu/article/donald-trump-boris-johnson-kiss-mural-brexit-referendum-leave-remain/}}</ref><ref name=\":22\">{{cite |last=McTague |first=Tom |date=4 October 2021 |title=Is Boris Johnson a Liar? |url=https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2021/10/boris-johnson/620269/ |access-date=18 October 2021 |website=The Atlantic}}</ref> He has been considered a figure with broad appeal outside of the usual Conservative support base.{{sfn|Edwards|Isaby|2008|p=47}} Johnson's premiership has been described by historians as the most controversial and scandal-affected since that of [[David Lloyd George]] about a century earlier.<ref name=\"Observer-historians\">{{cite news |title=The most controversial PM since Lloyd George: historians on Boris Johnson |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2022/sep/04/the-most-controversial-pm-since-lloyd-george-historians-on-boris-johnson |access-date=4 September 2022 |work=[[The Observer]] |date=4 September 2022}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nSince Johnson was born in New York City to British parents, he first held [[British Americans|British-American]] [[dual citizenship]]. In 2014, he acknowledged he was disputing a demand for [[capital gains tax]] from the [[Internal Revenue Service|US tax authorities]] on a property that he inherited in the United Kingdom,<ref name=\"telegraph-20141120\">{{cite news |last=Watt |first=Holly |date=20 November 2014 |title=Boris Johnson could be hit with six-figure tax bill |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/politics/london-mayor-election/mayor-of-london/11243742/Boris-Johnson-could-be-hit-with-six-figure-tax-bill.html |url-status=live |work=The Daily Telegraph |location=London |archive-url=https://archive.today/2014.11.21-131746/http://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/politics/london-mayor-election/mayor-of-london/11243742/Boris-Johnson-could-be-hit-with-six-figure-tax-bill.html |archive-date=21 November 2014 |access-date=5 May 2021 |url-access=limited}}</ref><ref name=\"guardian-20141120\">{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2014/nov/20/boris-johnson-us-tax-bill |title=New York-born London mayor Boris Johnson refuses to pay US tax bill |last=Siddique |first=Haroon |work=The Guardian |location=London |date=20 November 2014 |access-date=21 November 2014 |archive-date=6 February 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210206064813/https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2014/nov/20/boris-johnson-us-tax-bill |url-status=live}}</ref> which ultimately he paid.<ref name=\"bbc-20150122\">{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-30932891 |title=London Mayor Boris Johnson agrees to pay US tax bill |work=BBC News |date=22 January 2015 |access-date=15 February 2015 |archive-date=16 February 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150216123246/http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-30932891 |url-status=live}}</ref> In February 2015, he announced his intention to renounce his US citizenship to demonstrate his loyalty to the UK,<ref>{{cite news |last=Shipman |first=Tim |date=15 February 2015|title=Crikey! Boris gives up White House to bid for No 10|work=[[The 2016.<ref name=\"guardian-8\u2013february\">{{cite web |last=Wintour |first=Patrick |title=Boris Johnson among record number to renounce American citizenship in 2016 February 2017 |archive-date=22 July 2019 |url-status=live}}</ref> Johnson has a knowledge of French, Italian, German, Spanish,{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=109}} [[Latin]], and [[Ancient Greek]],<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.irishtimes.com/news/reading-into-the-problem-of-illiteracy-where-street-is-often-king-1.625047 |title=Reading into the problem of illiteracy where 'Street' is often king employing and alluding to [[Classics|classical]] references in both his newspaper columns and his speeches.{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=91}} His favourite film is ''[[The Godfather]]'', owing to \"the multiple retribution killings at the end\".<ref name=\"veconomist\" >{{cite news|date=20 February 2020|title=Britain's imperial prime minister|url=https://www.economist.com/britain/2020/02/22/britains-imperial-prime-minister|newspaper=[[The 2021|url-access=subscription}}</ref>\n\n[[Sonia Purnell]] wrote that Johnson was a \"highly evasive figure\" when it came to his personal life,{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=1}} who remained detached from others and who had very few if any intimate friends.{{sfn|Purnell|2011|p=15}} Among friends and family, Johnson is more commonly known as Al (short for his forename Alexander), rather than his middle name Boris.{{sfnm|1a1=Edwards|1a2=Isaby|1y=2008|1p=43|2a1=Purnell|2y=2011|2p=1|3a1=Gimson|3y=2012|3p=xiii}}\n\nIn 2007, Johnson said he had smoked [[cannabis]] before he went to university.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.oxfordmail.co.uk/news/1446705.boris_i_took_cocaine_and_cannabis/ |title=Boris: I took cocaine and cannabis |date=4 June 2007 |work=[[Oxford Mail]] |access-date=8 October 2012 also said he had used [[cocaine]].{{sfn|Edwards|Isaby|2008|pp=144\u2013145}} Johnson partakes in [[cycling]], [[tennis]] and [[pilates]], and was formerly an avid [[Jogging|runner]] before having to give it up owing to knee problems.<ref name=\":5\">{{Cite web |date=6 April 2020 |title=Hospital admission puts new focus on Boris Johnson's health weight has fluctuated throughout his career; he was considered [[obese]] in 2018 and [[overweight]] in 2020, and has spoken of making efforts to lose weight.<ref name=\":5\" /><ref>{{Cite web }}</ref>\n\nJohnson owns a \u00a31.3 million buy-to-let townhouse in [[Camberwell]], South London. According to [[HM Land Registry]] documents, he bought the four-bedroom property with his then-girlfriend [[Carrie Symonds]] in July 2019. The register of MPs' interests states that Johnson has a rental income of at least \u00a310,000 a year.<ref>{{Cite Since he was baptised Catholic, but his previous weddings were not conferred by the Catholic Church, they are considered putatively invalid.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Southworth |first1=Phoebe The pair did not comment; shortly afterward, Johnson employed Fazackerley.{{sfnm|1a1=Purnell|1y=2011|1pp=296\u2013300|2a1=Gimson|2y=2012|2pp=255\u2013257}}<ref name=\"auto\" />\n\nIn 2009, Johnson fathered a daughter with Helen Macintyre, an arts consultant. In 2013, the [[Court of Appeal of England and Wales|Court of Appeal]] discharged an injunction banning reporting of his daughter's existence. Johnson's stepmother, Jenny, the second wife of his father Stanley, is the stepdaughter of [[Joseph Sieff|Teddy Sieff]], the former chairman of [[Marks & Spencer]].<ref>{{cite news beauties|slave]] origin.{{sfnm|1a1=Edwards|1a2=Isaby|1y=2008|1p=44|2a1=Purnell|2y=2011|2pp=19\u201320|3a1=Gimson|3y=2012|3pp=5\u20137, 1957}}<ref>{{cite news |last=Acar |first=\u00d6zgen |date=20 June
